was\n\nvariable\nof\n\nspacing.\n\ndetails\n\nto\nwithin\nof\n\nFour high-performance prototype converters were fabricated during\nTask II and the performance goal of 20 watts/cm 2 power output at 0.8\nvolts for an emitter temperature of 1735\xc2\xb0C (true) was achieved\xc2\xb0 The\ninterelectrode spacings of these converters were selected for specific\noutput characteristics\nfrom the data acquired from the parametric test\nvehicles of Task I. A significant achievement of the program was the\nexact correlation between the performances of the prototype converters\nand the parametric vehicles.\nThe prototype converters of Task II were\nfabricated using a new fabrication method developed during the program,\nwherein prefabricated subassemblies, including metal-ceramic seals, were\nelectron beamwelded together to form the final converter assembly\xc2\xb0\nThis modular approach is inherently highly reliable since the final step\nin the converter assembly is a metal-to-metal joint rather than a seal\nbraze. The converters and their fabrication are discussed in Section 4.\nThe Task II investigations in fabrication technology are discussed\nin detail in Section 3. Briefly, the results were:\nI. An electron beamwelding schedule was developed which permitted\na reliable weld between a solid rhenium emitter and rhenium\nenvelope. Two test vehicles and four thermionic converters\nutilized this weld schedule without failure or reweld.\n2_ A seal testing program demonstrated that active brazed, metalto-ceramic seals can withstand hundreds of thermal cycles at\na cycle rate of 100\xc2\xb0C/min. Moreover, it was established\nthat those seals could be prefabricated\nwelded to tile converter structures.\n\nand then electron beam\n\n3. geometry\n\nutilizes\na concentric guard ring and a collector barrel with exposed\nemitter.\nFigure 2-6 shows the geometry of the vehicle.\nAn added\nbenefit of this design is the elimination of a "parasitic"\ncesium\nreservoir which occurs when a location within the device approaches\nthe reservoir temperature. By keeping the vehicle compact, with the\nbellows, seals, and guard ring concentric to the collector barrel,\nthe device proper will operate at least 150\xc2\xb0Chigher than the reservoir.\nThe length of the collector barrel is determined by\nboth heat transfer considerations and, mechanically, the fact that it\nmust be coaxial with a guard ring of a particular\n\nlength.\n\nThe length\n\nof the guard ring is mainly set by the mechanical limitations which\nare introduced by the requirement that the guard ring-collector\nmust\nmovewith respect to the emitter and emitter envelope.\n2.2.1.1\n\nVariable\n\nParameter\n\nTest\n\nVehicle\n\nThermal\n\nAnalysis\nA\ndesign\n\nof the\n\nbutions\n\nemission\n\nand,\n\nreduce\n\nfiT in\n\nvehicle\n\ncontact\n\n(zero\n\nbarrel\n\nprimary\n\npotential)\n\nat\n\nthe\n\nthe\n\nsame\n\ntime,\n\ncollector\n\nhave\n\ncontact\n\npotential\n\nmaterial,\nthe\n\nequal\n\nor nearly\n\nconsider\n\ncollector\n\nthe\n\nbarrel\n\nthe\n\nQcoll\nthermal\n\nsectional\n\n6952-Final\n\nis\n\nthe\n\nof\n\nthe\n\ntemperature\n\nthe\n\ncollector\nheat\n\nring\n\nthe\n\ncollector\n\nbarrel\n\nguard\n\ngradients\nare\n\nand\n\ndistri-\n\nlength\n\nto\n\nfluxes.\n\nwhether\n\nthey\n\nthermal\n\nand\n\nfabricated\n\nderivation.\n\nThe\n\ndT\n_x\n\nring\nhence\nof\n\nheat\n\nthe\n\nand\n\ncol-\n\nzero\nsame\n\nconducted\n\nI\n! The heat sink consists of 1-inch copper straps,\ni/8-inch thick, which are connected to copper bus bars by flexible\ncopper straps. The bus bars have been fitted with copper tubing which\ncan be used for air or water cooling to accomplish a variable thermal\nconduction. An experiment was conducted to determine the heat\ntransfer characteristics\nof such a mechanically clamped collectorradiator combination. Figure 2-7 shows the experimental arrangement\nand the position of thermocouples. the\nthermal power conducted down the rhenium heat choke is 86 watts, the\njoule heating power generated in the heat choke is 33 watts, and the\npower radiated by the envelope is 9 watts. Therefore, the total power\nlost by the emitter down the rhenium envelope is 62 watts for an\nemitter temperature of 1700\xc2\xb0Cand an emitter current of 250 amperes.\nFor tantalum, the thermal power conducted down the heat choke is 80\nwatts, the joule heating power generated in the envelope is 31 watts,\nand the radiated power is Ii watts. Then the total power drained from\nthe emitter by a tantalum heat choke envelope is 60 watts for an\nemitter temperature of 1700\xc2\xb0C and an emitter current of 250 conto detail\n\ncalibrated\n\nagainst\n\nan NBS certified\n\nstandard lamp before, during,\n\nand immediately after\n\nthe test vehicle operation. The pyrometers were of the micro-optical\ntype with bulb filaments approximately one-sixth the diameter of the\nblackbody holes sighted upon. The thermocouples consisted of continuous wire from the surface being measured through the vacuumstation\nport and ending in a 0\xc2\xb0C ice bath. Potential leads were attached at\nthe device terminals with wire of the samematerial as the terminal to\ninsure that no thermal emf was generated.\nThe principal purpose of the variable\n\nparameter test\n\nvehicle was to obtain thermionic converter optimization\nlarly as a function of spacing between the electrodes.\n\ndata, particuIn addition,\n\nand perhaps of equal importance, the test vehicle offers a measurement\nof basic plasma parameters such as the pressure-distance product. The\nparagraphs that follow contain the results of over 450 I-V characteristics and ii00 dc, steady-state data points yielding the most definitive characterization of thermionic performance known to date.\n2.2.5.1\n\nConverter\nOptimization\nData\nRhenium\nElectrode\nSystem\nThe\n\nmizing\n\nthe\n\ndc\n\ncurrent\n\ncesium\n\ntemperature,\n\nand\n\nperature\n\nof\n\n0.6\n\nas measured\n\nvolt\n\nprocedure\nstant\n\nin\n\nature\n\nand\noutput\n\nwas\n\n596\xc2\xb0C,\nthe\n\nat\n\n610\xc2\xb0C,\n\nupper\n\n6952-Final\n\nthe\n\ntest\n\nthe\n\nreservoir\n\nbetween\n\n310\xc2\xb0C\n\nspacing\n\nwas\n\nwas\nand\n\ncollector\n\nrepeated\n660\xc2\xb0C.\nsurface\n\na fixed\n\nterminals.\n\nThe\n\nload\n\ncollector\n\nand\n\nThe\n\n350\xc2\xb0C.\nbetween\n\ncollector\n\nCollector\n\nroot\n\nimmersion\n\n45\n\nAt\n\nroot\n\n0.7\n\nan\n\neach\n\nare\nopened\n\nfixed\nmaxitemper-\n\ncollector\n\n0.005\n\ntemperatures\n\nthermocouple\n\na con-\n\nabsolute\n\nfixed\n\ntemperatures\n\nand\n\nexperimental\n\nreservoir\n\nand\n\ntem-\n\nvolt,\n\ntemperature,\n\ncesium\n\n0.002\n\nspacing,\n\nto maintain\n\nuntil\n\nopti-\n\nemitter\n\nvolt_\n\nobtained.\n\nRhenium-\n\nof\n\nof\n\na true\n\n0.8\n\ntemperature\n\nvaried\nfor\n\nof\n\nthe\n\nconsisted\n\na function\nat\n\nan electronic\n\nvarying\n\nbeen\n\nas\n\noutputs\n\nvehicle\n\nemploying\n\nhad\n\nvehicle\n\nvoltage\n\nsetting\n\ncurrent\n\noptimization\n\ntemperature,\n\nand\n\nthe\n\nprocedure\n\nthe\n\ncollector\n\nthree\n\nof\n\nof\n\noutput\n\nvaried\n\ntemperature,\nThis\n\nat\n\nconsisted\n\nspacing,\nmum\n\n1735\xc2\xb0C\n\nvoltage\n\noutput\n\nconverter\n\nfor\n\ninch.\nof\n\n570\xc2\xb0C,\n\nquoted\n\nsince\n\nduring\n\nthe\n\nfirst few hours of vacuumoutgassing. Fig.\n\nDIAGRAM\nDEVELOPED\n2-27)\n\n65\n\nFOR\n\nSPACE-CHARGE,\n\nPLASMA\n\nAT\n\nTHE\n\ndc\n\nINCIPIENT\nPOINTS\n\nA,\n\nbe seen in Fig. 2-28, the dc operating point for point B occurs\ndirectly at ignition.\nThis operating point is very unstable since\nthe constant current point can occur at two different voltages. Compared to point A_ the voltage output has decreased to allow for the\naccelerating potential distribution\nfor electrons into the anode. A\nplasma has not developed yet, but as this potential approaches the\nfirst excitation potential for cesium, the ionization mechanismscan\nbe optimized. This process continues until point C is reached. At\nthis point, a fully developed plasma exists, as typified by the potential diagram of point C in Fig. 2-28. In all of the potential diagrams of Fig. 2-28, the plasma potential is assumedto be matched to\nthe anode for the sake of simplicity.\nReturning to the data at close spacing, a\npreliminary analysis was performed on the space charge region of the\nvoltage-spacing curve of Fig. 2-29. Fig.\n\nanalysis\n\nbe\n\nA\n\ndefinitely\n\ncontributions\n\nof\n\npoint\n\nis\n\nthe\n\nthe\n\ncan\n\nvehicle\n\nregion\n\nvoltage\n\nthe\n\nto\n\nto\n\nexperimental\n\ndifferentiation\n\nrepresents\n\ninfluence\n\nbeyond\n\ncolumn\n\nin\n\nof\n\nin:\n\ndVcathode\ndx\n\n2-29\n\naccuracy\n\nvolts/cm\n\npoint-by-point\n\nsince\n\nresults\n\n512\n\napplies\n\nlimited\n\nshown\n\nadditional\n\nobservation\n\ndVout/dx\n\nis\n\nintensity\n\n2-12\n\ndVout\ndx\n\ncurve\n\n2-26\n\nthe\n\nthe\n\nA\ncurve\n\nExperimental\n\nvolts/cm\n\nlaw\n\nspacings\n\ninch\n\n2-14\n\nwithin\n\nChilds-Langmuir\n\n2-VI\n\nthe\n\nterms.\n\nconstant\n\nfor\n\nof\n\na posi-\n\ninterelectrode\n\nconditions\n\nstated.\n\nMeasurements\n\nfrom\n\nRhenium\ncesiated\nwere\n\nwork\n\nobtained\n\nfunction\nby\n\nthe\n\nmeasure-\n\ncombined\n\ndc and ac method. This method is utilized\n\nsince it\n\ntraces an instan-\n\ntaneous characteristic\nat fixed parameter temperatures. The dc operating point is usually set by an electronic load. The sweep transformer\nthen sweeps out a portion of the I-V characteristic\naround this dc\npoint after it is ascertained that the element temperature, particularly the emitter, maintains the samevalue. Collected current is\ndetermined by measuring the voltage drop across a calibrated,\n\n0.1-\n\npercent-accurate shunt and displayed on the y-axis of an x-y scope.\nApplied voltage or generated voltage is measureddirectlv across the\ntest vehicle terminals and displayed on the x-axis of the oscilloscope.\nTo accurately determine saturated emission, it is sometimesnecessary\nto sweep the arc voltage as much as 2 volts into the applied voltage\nquadrant. Since the zener diodes in the electronic load cannot hold\noff more than 0.5 volts in the forward direction,\nthe electronic load\nwas replaced by a resistive\n\nload across the test vehicle and a low\n\ninductance, low impedance, secondary stepdown transformer employed as\na sweep source. The saturated emission is defined as the intersection\nof the extrapolated Schottky slope and the slope of the plasma region.\nFigure 2-30 consists of three I-V characteristics\nwith an applied\nvoltage of between 1.5 and 2.0 volts.\nTo insure that the saturated\nelectron emission is independent of interelectrode spacing, three\nspacings were selected for emission measurement: 0.001, 0.003, and\n0.006 inch. The characteristics\nshowthat the measured saturated\nemission was constant within i 5 percent for the sameconditions\nemitter\nof six.\n\nand reservoir\n\nof\n\ntemperature while the spacing varied by a factor\n\nExact determination of temperature is a very\nimportant part of accurate electron emission measurements. For all\ntemperature determinations, other than the emitter and collector,\ncalibrated Chromel-Alumel thermocouples traceable to the National\nBureau of Standards were used. i_\n\n6952-Final\n\n_O_i]OA\n\n89\n\nIn either case, the rate of diffusion is highly dependent upon the\ncollector surface temperature. The length of time required to deplete\nthe surface would depend upon the initial\namount present on the surface, the, rate of diffusion,\nand the rate of replacement from the\nemitter.\nSince there is almost an absolute lack of diffusion data\nfor these systems, and particularly\nfor thin coatings, it was felt\nthat the\' balance (_f data taking should be conducted on stable surfaces\nto eliminate possible concern that the test vehicle itself was failing\nor that the drive mechanismhad becomefaulty.\nThe collector surface\nwas therefore replenished with evaporated rhenium from the emitter\noperating at 2100\xc2\xb0Cwith the cesium reservoir heaters secured. The\ncollector work function, after this processing, was determined to be\n1.45 to 1.43 eV which agrees quite well with the work function determinations from the rhenium-rhenium test vehicle.\nThe average difference of 0.080 volt from these successive measurementsalso corresponds\nto the voltage output lost in the spacing-voltage curves.\n\nThis safne\n\nphenomenon\nwas later observed in a rhenium-molybdenumthermionic converter wherein the converter optimization data for "both the rheniummolybdenumand rhenium-rhenium/molybdenumsystems was carefully documented and once again, a difference of 0.080 volt in performance output was noted (see Section 5).\nBefore proceeding to the converter optimization data, a voltage output versus spacing curve was obtained for 38\namperes fixed current level and the initial\ndata of the test vehicle\nwas reproduced within 3 to 4 millivolts\nthroughout the entire range of\nspacing. In addition, a voltage-spacing curve at 60 ampereswas\nobtained which reproduced Fig\xc2\xb0 2-27 within 5 millivolts\nover the entire spacing range from 0_0002 inch to 0\xc2\xb0009 inch\xc2\xb0 These data further\nsubstantiated the rhenium nature of the collector surface after the\nevaporation o \'1OO8\n\n8OID3llOD\n\n(]NV\n\n3DV_SfIS 8OID377OD\nN33/V_I38\n3DN383_31G\n38rllV83dW31\n\'1S7\n\n6952-Final\n\n107\n\nSix pinch-offs were madewith two different hand\ntools (Varian and Kane). The pinch-offs were then cross-sectioned,\nand examined for seal thickness.\nOf the six pinch-offs, only one had\na seal thickness greater than 0.005 inch, the rest were 0.001 inch or\nless. Figures 3-7 and 3-8 show micro-sections of these marginal\nseals. In general, the hand tools required contin.ot_s adjustmen_ to\ninsure that the rollers mated properly.\nThe rollers,\nthough casehardened, require periodic replacement.\n\nMoreover, the actual pincll\n\noperation using a hand tool is dependent upon the steadiness and skill\nof the operator.\nSix additional\n\npinch-offs\n\nwere madefrom the same\n\nlength of sample tubing. The tool used for these pinch-offs was a\nKanehydraulic tool having I/4-inch and i/8-inch diameter, fully\nhardened tool-steel rollers.\nAll pinch-off samples were examined for\nseal thickness and were found to vary between 0.006 inch and 0.009\ninch with no preference for roller\n\ndiameter (Figs. 3-9 and 3-10).\n\nThe\n\nhydraulic tool requires only initial\nadjustment and o_casional readjustment; the rollers appear to be capable of lasting almost indefinitely and the pinch-off operation proceeds with a smooth stroke,\nindependent of operator skill or experience.\nA few general observations on pinch-off procedures\nare outlined below which, if followed, should lead to consistent,\nhighly reliable OFHC\ncopper tubing pinch-offs.\ni. The copper (OFHC)must be first chemically cleaned to remove\nall contamination induced by mill handling.\n2. The copper must be annealed (after chemical cleaning) in a\nhigh-vacuum environment at temperatures in the 700\xc2\xb0C area\nfor 1/2 hour.\n3.\n\nThe pinch area should be preflattened\nand re-annealed.\n\n4.\n\nThe pinch-off rollers or jaws should be madeof fully treated\ntool steel and they should be periodically\nchecked for evidence of warpage or misalignment.\n\n6952-Final\n\n108\n\nwith a flattening\n\ntool\n\nFIG\n\n3-7\n\nANNEALED OFHC COPPER TUBING\n1/4" O.D.\n0.030" WALL. emitter\n\nenvelope subassembly is comprised of a\n\nrhenium envelope, a niobium transition ring, and tantalum lead straps.\nAll parts are vanadium-brazed. The niobium transition ring contains\na 0.060-inch-thick\nlip section to which the upper flange of the prefabricated seal is electron-beam welded.\nThe final assembly operation is the electron-beam\nwelding of the rhenium emitter to the envelope subassembly. The weld\nschedule follows the parameters established from the secondary experiments, that is, an electron-beam voltage of 150 kV at a current of\n4.9 mA, with a part revolution speed of 40 rpmo Attaching the emitter\nlast has several advantages: (i) It allows for visual inspection of\nthe concentricity of the envelope and collector,\n(2) It permits a high\ntemperature emitter outgas and grain stabilization\ntreatment independent\nof the converter structure.\nIn particular,\nthe outgassed emitter impurities will contaminate the collector surface and prevent an optimum\ncesiated work function during converter operation, (3) It provides a\nmeansof setting the interelectrode spacing to e predetermined value\nby grinding\n\nor shaping the emitter before welding.\nThe final diode is depicted in Fig. 4-4. As noted,\nonly three electron-beam welds are necessary for assembly -- two welds\nat the flanges and one at the emitter.\nThe exhaust tubulation is joined\nto the diode assembly, and high
